The arm is composed of two bones, which are called "forks"; one small, and it is the one that bears the foot, and the other large, which holds the small one below from the beginning upwards.
And if the larger fork is easily broken, or the smaller one, and both are easily fractured.
And when the small fork is broken below, then the restoration of it is lighter, and the healing of it is even lighter.
And when the larger fork is broken below the fracture of it is bad, and the healing of it is difficult.
And worse still when both bones are broken at the same time.
Therefore if the bone that is broken is the smaller fork below, then it is convenient for the doctor to perform the restoration of it, as a short pause in extension, with ease, until it is encased.

Chapter XXIII.
On the cause of dislocation.
Dislocation occurs when one of the joints in the body is injured, and therefore it must be prohibited from movement, and the figure of the limb is twisted, and brings over the patient intense pain and large injuries.
Therefore, when a dislocation occurs, one must promptly attempt to reduce it, and not delay in doing so, because if it is delayed, the joint becomes swollen and strong with this, and it is done difficult to reduce the dislocation.
And so it is not necessary to be swollen or extended in the hour of the operation, because many times we have seen that spasms and pains arise afterwards.
When such accidents happen, it is necessary to get back into the bowels of the disease, and so place the opening in such a way that you pause the swelling; and so the member should be bound with hot water and oil, and so it should be reduced with ease.
And the whole member will be healed with that of which the memory comes back to its place.
And I have ordered the capitals of dislocation according to what has been preceded in fracture; from the top of the bone above to the bottom on the left side.
